25:T2d30,<entryFree id="n12246" key="دَخَلَ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <itype>1</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">دَخَلَ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">دخل</orth>
                  </form>, (S, K, &amp;c.,) aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bu" lang="ar">دَخُلَ</orth>
                  </form>, (TA,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">دُخُولٌ</foreign> (S, Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">مَدْخَلٌ</foreign>, (S, K,) <hi rend="ital">He,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, entered;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">went, came, passed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">got, in; contr. of</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">خَرَجَ</foreign>; (K;) as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n12246-1" target="اِدَّخَلَ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, of the measure <foreign lang="ar">اِفْتَعَلَ</foreign>, and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n12246-2" target="اندخل" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, (S, K,) this last occuring in poetry, but not chaste, (S,) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n12246-3" target="تدخّل" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n12246"/></foreign>, (K,) or this signifies <hi rend="ital">it</hi> (a thing) <hi rend="ital">entered by little and little.</hi> (S, O.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">دَخَلْتُ مَدْخَلًا حَسَنًا</foreign> [like <foreign lang="ar">دُخُولًا حَسَنًا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">I entered with a good entering</hi>]. (S.) And <foreign lang="ar">دَخَلْتُ البَيْتَ</foreign> (S) or <foreign lang="ar">الدَّارَ</foreign>, i. e. [<hi rend="ital">I entered the house,</hi> or] <hi rend="ital">I became within the house,</hi> and the like, (Msb,) correctly meaning <foreign lang="ar">إِلَى البَيْتِ</foreign> [&amp;c., or <foreign lang="ar">فِى البَيْتِ</foreign> &amp;c., i. e. <hi rend="ital">I entered into the house,</hi> &amp;c.], the prep. being suppressed, and the noun put in the accus. case after the manner of an objective complement: for nouns of place are of two kinds, vague and definite; the vague being such as the six relative locations, <foreign lang="ar">خَلْفٌ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">قُدَّامٌ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">يَمِينٌ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">شِمَالٌ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">فَوْقٌ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">تَحْتٌ</foreign>, and the like, such as <foreign lang="ar">أَمَامٌ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">وَرَآءٌ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">أَعْلَى</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">أَسْفَلُ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">عِنْدَ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">لَدُنْ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">وَسْطٌ</foreign> in the sense of <foreign lang="ar">بَيْنٌ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">قُبَالَةٌ</foreign>, all which, and similar nouns of place, may become adverbs, because indefinite; for dost thou not see that what is <foreign lang="ar">خَلْف</foreign> to thee may be <foreign lang="ar">قُدَّام</foreign> to another? but that which is definite, having make, and corporeal substance, and tracts that comprehend it, as a mountain and a valley and a market and a house and a mosque, the noun signifying such a thing cannot become an adverb; for you may not say, <foreign lang="ar">قَعَدْتُ الدَّارَ</foreign>, nor <foreign lang="ar">صَلَّيْتُ المَسْجِدَ</foreign>, nor <foreign lang="ar">نِمْتُ الجَبَلَ</foreign>, nor <foreign lang="ar">قُمْتُ الوَادِىَ</foreign>; the phrases of this kind that occur being instances of the suppression of a prep.; as <foreign lang="ar">دَخَلْتُ البَيْتَ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">نَزَلْتُ الوَادِىَ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">صَعِدْتُ الجَبَلَ</foreign>. (S, O, TA.) You say also, <foreign lang="ar">دَخَلْتُ عَلَى زَيْدٍ الدَّارَ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">I entered the house after Zeyd, he being in it.</hi> (Msb.) [And simply <foreign lang="ar">دَخَلَ عَلَيْهِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He came in upon him:</hi> and also <hi rend="ital">he came upon him;</hi> i. e. <hi rend="ital">invaded him.</hi>] And <foreign lang="ar">دَخَلَ بِٱمْرَأَتِهِ</foreign>, (Msb, TA,) and <foreign lang="ar">عَلَيْهَا</foreign>, (MA,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">دُخُولٌ</foreign>, (Mgh, Msb,) [like <foreign lang="ar">دَخَلَ بِأَهْلِهِ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">عَلَيْهَا</foreign>, (see <foreign lang="ar">أَهْلٌ</foreign>,) i. e. <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">He went in to his wife</hi> or <hi rend="ital">woman,</hi>] is a metonymical phrase, denoting <foreign lang="ar">الجِمَاع</foreign>, (Msb, TA,) i. e. <foreign lang="ar">الوَطْء</foreign>, (Mgh, Msb, TA,) whether it be such as is allowed by the law or such as is forbidden, (Mgh,) generally such as is lawful. (Msb, TA. [See what is said in explanation of the term <foreign lang="ar">خَلْوَةٌ</foreign> in the first paragraph of art. <foreign lang="ar">خلو</foreign>.]) And <foreign lang="ar">دَخَلَ بَعْضُهُ فِى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بَعْضٍ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">i. q.</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">تَدَاخَلَ</foreign> [q. v.]. (TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">قصر</foreign>, &amp;c.) [For ex.,] you say, <foreign lang="ar">دَخَلَ بَعْضُ النُّجُومِ فِى بَعْضٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The stars became confused together</hi>]. (Mgh and TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">شبك</foreign>: in the former coupled with <foreign lang="ar">اِخْتَلَطَتْ</foreign>.) And <foreign lang="ar">دَخَلَ فِيهِمْ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He entered among them, so as to become a member of their community, confraternity, party, sect,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the like;</hi>] said of a stranger. (K.) [And <foreign lang="ar">دَخَلَ فِى طَاعَتِهِ</foreign>: see <foreign lang="ar">طَائِعٌ</foreign>, in art. <foreign lang="ar">طوع</foreign>.] When <foreign lang="ar">دَخَلَ</foreign> is said of income, or revenue, [meaning <hi rend="ital">It came in, accrued,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">was received,</hi>] the aor. is as above, and the inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">دَخْلٌ</foreign>: (Msb:) and you say, <foreign lang="ar">يَدْخُلُ عَلَى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الإِنْسَانِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">It comes in,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">accrues, to the man</hi>]. (Msb, K. *) <foreign lang="ar">دَخَلَ بِهِ</foreign> [lit. <hi rend="ital">He entered with him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it</hi>]: see 4.          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  [Hence, <foreign lang="ar">دَخَلَ فِيهِ</foreign> meaning <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">It became included, comprehended,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">comprised, in it.</hi> And hence,] <foreign lang="ar">دَخَلَ فِى دِينِ الإِسْلَامِ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  [<hi rend="ital">He entered within the pale of the religion of ElIslám; he entered the communion of that religion; he entered into, embraced,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became a proselyte to, that religion</hi>]. (Msb in art. <foreign lang="ar">سلم</foreign>, &amp;c. [See Kur cx. 2.]) And <foreign lang="ar">دَخَلَ فِى الأَمْرِ</foreign>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">دُخُولٌ</foreign>, <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">He entered upon, began,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">commenced, the affair.</hi> (Msb.)
